The Tiger Knuckle is a punch aimed  at the jinchu, a pressure point     located between the nose and        mouth
This move delivers a downward       rotating blow from the forearms,    aimed at the opponent's collarbone
Unlike the Elbow Slam, this blow    is thrown horizontally in a         sweeping hook
The Elbow Assault targets the       center of the opponent's body       with a full-body rush
A move where the practitioner       momentarily lowers, then raises     his body and swings to strike the   opponent on the jaw
This move involves taking one step  forward with the rear leg and       punching at a mid-level target with the fist
The Rain Thrust is a straight       punch aimed at a pressure point     on the right side of the human      neck
The Big Wheel is a powerful         variation of the Elbow Slam. It is  aimed at the opponent's             collarbone, with a diagonal blow    struck after the practitioner            closes in
This move involves advancing a step forward and striking the opponent's chest and jaw with the palm and     entire forearm. The impact creates  a shockwave that affects the        opponent's internal organs
This is a surprise attack with a    spinning backfist. The spinning     motion increases the power          of the blow
This move strikes the pit of the    opponent's stomach with an elbow    bent at an acute angle like that of a lance thrust.  Experts can attack while spinning, to evade attacks
The practitioner advances one step  with the forward leg and delivers a slashing blow to the opponent's     side with the side of the palm
A move which utilizes the running   speed of the practitioner to delivera diagonal cutting blow to the area between the shoulder and the nape   of the neck
This double punch begins with a     step forward and a mid-level strike with the leading fist, and then a   second punch to the same target     with the other hand. Masters of     this move can add an elbow strike
The practitioner firmly places his  forward palm on the enemy's body,   plants himself, and slams the palm  of his free hand into the back of   his other hand in a devastating     blowThis advanced move from the Yang    Qing Style involves deflecting the  opponent's attack, and kicking the  opponent's legs at the same time.   It is a closely kept secret, and    not taught easily
A move where the practitioner       lowers his body momentarily, then   springs upward and delivers a blow  to the opponent's chin
The practitioner throws a chop to   the opponent's neck using the sides of his open hands. When the         technique is mastered, the          practitioner can repeat the attack  after the initial strike
Iwao Hazuki learned this move in    China. The practitioner strikes a   blow with the palm, using power     from a twist of the back. Experts   can make the blow even more         powerful by stepping in deeper
The Crescent Kick is unleashed like an upward sword-stroke, aimed at    the opponent's head
A so-called front kick, but the     kick is delivered using the entire  underside of the foot, and rather   than kicking out, a stamping action is employed. Targets the vital      points in the front of the body
This is a low, decisive kick aimed  at the outside of an opponent's     knee
With this flying knee kick move,    the practitioner leaps upward to    kick while restraining the opponent with both hands. Masters of this    move can increase its destructive   power
This back roundhouse kick strikes   in a diagonally downward motion     across the opponent's body. The     path of the kick resembles the      surplice worn by Buddhist monks
This kick begins as a high outside  spin kick, but ends as a heel drop. The path of the kick is compact,    and those who master the move       can follow a middle kick with this  technique
This move involves using the power  of the forward leg to deliver a low to mid-level kick to the opponent
This is a high-speed roundhouse     kick. Those who have not yet        mastered the move usually find      themselves off balance when they    miss, but experts can recover with  ease
A kick delivered while flipping     forward in mid-air, this is one of  the more unusual moves in the       Hazuki style. Experts leave no      openings for an attack after the    execution of this move
This jumping back roundhouse kick   is powerful, due to the jump and    rotation, but is also easy to dodge.Masters of the move can jump        higher to kick
A flying back kick, this powerful   move aims a diagonally slicing kick at the base of the opponent's neck
A move from the Yang Qing Style     also reminiscent of Taekwondo. The  initial kick is a feint, and after  the opponent is lured in, the       practitioner intercepts him with    the heel drop
A daring move which uses the        spinning momentum from the          first spin kick to spin again and   deliver a powerful second kick
Nothing Skill Information
With this move, the practitioner    lowers his body, spins around       rapidly on the pivot leg, and using the other leg, sweeps out the       legs from under his opponent
With this move, the practitioner    slides toward the opponent, and     kicks upward with the leg, aiming   for the abdomen. Experts can also   aim for the jaw
A simple flying kick, but in the    hands of an expert, a heel drop can be added after landing from the     first kick
While running, the practitioner     suddenly slides along the ground to sweep the feet out from under the   opponent. Experts can twist their   body to make the attack stronger
With this move, the practitioner    takes the opponent's arm and lowers his own body while grabbing the     opponent's collar, lifting him onto his back and throwing him
This throwing move involves quickly turning and pulling the opponent's  collar, then using the leg to sweep up the opponent's inner thigh and   throw him. In Judo, the move is     called |uchimata+
In this so-called sacrifice throw,  similar to the Judo technique,      the practitioner falls backward to  throw the opponent far to the rear
With this move, the practitioner    grabs the opponent's neck and       reaps the leg, applying power in    the opposite directions to the      upper and lower body
The practitioner uses an armlock    to throw the opponent, and also     flips forward in mid-air during the throw to land on the opponent
As the opponent attempts a strike,  the practitioner grasps the arm,    executes an armlock, and pins him.  A common technique in older         styles of jujitsu, this move varies from style to style
This dynamic move involves          lowering the body to grasp the      opponent's leg, lifting the         opponent onto the shoulders,        and dropping him headfirst by       toppling over sideways
This move involves closing in on    the opponent's side and throwing    him down while turning him 180      degrees. This technique is one of   the major Hazuki throws, and dates  back to the early days of the style
Similar to the back drop of         pro wrestling, it has been devised  to make it more difficult to defend against. The throw is executed by   including a twist toward the rear
A move involving the evasion of an  opponent's attack and moving behind him to arrive at his blind spot
A complex move that damages the     opponent's arms in multiple areas   simultaneously. When executed by    one who has mastered the technique, the opponent is left wondering what happened to them
The practitioner momentarily lowers his body and gathers his strength   to aggressively lunge into the      opponent. Experts can add a         shoulder strike after the initial   impact
This move is an extension of the    Shadow Step. After stepping into    the opponent's blind spot, the      practitioner strikes his neck
This is a combined defensive        and offensive move where the        practitioner evades an opponent's   attack diagonally, then moves in    for an elbow strike
